<h2>All Reviews</h2>

    <li> bought this one to replace an older model that broke, so far works really well.</li>
    <li> Shaves smooth  easy to clean  light in the hand.  I would give it 5 stars but it does not have a warning light to let you know how much battery is left.</li>
    <li> It cuts pretty good and close for an electric shaver. Better than my past electric models.&lt;br /&gt;It&#x27;s charge has lasted a few shaves now and still going strong. So, I gave it the fourth star.&lt;br /&gt;it don&#x27;t beat a straight razor for smoothness. Had it about a month now.</li>
    <li> it is best for shaving your head. i like it as slick bald as i can get it and this cuts closer than a blade with no nicks, no shaving cream. not as good on the face</li>
    <li> I&#x27;ve used Norelco shavers for over 30 years.  I was convinced to try a Braun shaver - expensive with great ratings.  A disaster.  The Norelco is quiet, simple and best of all gives a great shave.  This is a great shaver at a great price.</li>
    <li> I had this shaver for a couple years, and then it caught on fire while I was using it. No kidding. Smoke started coming out of the top of it while I was shaving.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;And it never really shaved that well to begin with.</li>
    <li> Super product.  Works great on my legs (female).  Do not spend more than you have to buying a shaver for women.</li>
    <li> I waited a few months to write a review on this because I had heard about the battery life going down after a few months of use, however, this report of the battery life I found was completely false. I&#x27;ve had this unit since March and the battery still lasts as long as the day I received it, I recently went on a 3 week business trip for work and forgot the charger cord and it lasted the whole trip on one full charge. The only complaint I have is that the pop up trimmer isn&#x27;t positioned on the unit so that you can be precise but that&#x27;s a small price to pay for the rest the unit has to offer. I personally believe it gives a closer shave than my old 4 blade razor. Excellent shaver for the price. Can&#x27;t be beat!</li>
    <li> My husband is home bound so this is great for him.  He shaves every day and I like the fact that it can be rinsed in hot water.</li>
    <li> Works great and price is reasonable. Am replacing an old one that lasted a long time.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Why pay big bucks for razors that provide almost not additional performance.</li>
    <li> This is a birthday gift for my husband. He likes it so much. The only concern I have it this model does have a stand for the shaver; it would be much nicer if the shaver can stand on the bathroom counter.</li>
    <li> I am actually a barber and i need to buy one of these a little more often than the average person that uses it for personal use. I only stay with the NORELCO brand tho. I like their products and they always last. This one from the gate gives a really smooth shave. I have been using it for 2 months straight, 5 days a week on people and the blades are still sharp. If it lasts me a year or two for my job, then it can last like up to 5 years for personal use. Definitely a good buy!</li>
    <li> Dissappointing from previous Norelco shavers owned. Very slow charge, simply acceptable performance. Go for the upper mid-level price shavers.</li>
    <li> Very good for travels. Could be easier to clean inside, but does a very good job. I recommend.</li>
    <li> This shaver is the reason I won&#x27;t ever buy a shaver from Philips Norelco.  This is the second one I bought. When I bought this one I thought Philips would have improved the shaver. The problem: you will need, good luck, the instructions,  a magnifying glass, and a close-up shot of the shaver heads, once you open the top and the heads and entire assembly falls out. And if you don&#x27;t have those items, good luck trying to reassemble the shaver head.  Philips could easily have made an easy to re-assemble shaver. The assembly in this one is plastic junk.    Do not buy this shaver.</li>
    <li> An excellent shaver.  Cuts close with minimum passes, a trimmer that is easy to use, and easy to clean under warm running water.  Comfortable and secure in the hand.  About two weeks between charges.  Cordless, but if the battery dies during a shave, can be used corded.  Nice compact charger, selects right voltage automatically, so great for international travel. So much better than the Remington MS2-390 I ditched after just a few months.  I would definitely recommend this rotary Norelco over the foil Remington.    A couple of minor niggles; first, no carry case - so I&#x27;ll be using that from my old Norelco that served me well for about eight years; and charge time on this new one is about eight hours - but only 40 mins on the old Norelco - is this really progress?!  Include a case and faster charge and I&#x27;d give it a 5 star.</li>
    <li> I have been shaving with a blade for over forty years, and since retirement I now don&#x27;t shave everyday. (Just me and my teenage son here.)  Some years back I tried a budget foil shaver that torn half my face off, and later a budget rotary that was not much better.  I decided to read some reviews on some expensive rotary shavers (not that I intended to spend $200+ for one) and found that all the bells and whistles on the latest models (from reviews) were more of a hassle than help.  I then started looking at reviews on some moderately priced units and came across one review on the 7310 that said: \\&quot;Norelco had it right years ago and then ruined it\\&quot;.  I gave it a try and it has only been a month but so far I have been very happy with the shave.  It is quiet, and shaves me as close as a blade.  I have to go over my neck a couple of times (whiskers grow sideways) but I had to do that with a blade.  My 17yr. old son tried it and now I will probably have to buy him one, and he has been using those fancy and expensive 5 blade Gillette razors.  I only write a review if an item is really bad or pretty good.  This item is pretty good and I would have given it 5 stars except after about 10 days it stopped halfway.  I recharged it and it is humming again, but there should be a red warning light, although I kinda knew it was ready for a charge.  I would recommend this shaver.</li>
    <li> I shaved with this for the first time yesterday. I had about 3 days worth of whiskers and it easily cut them. My prior razor was also a Norelco and I owned it for at least 3 years. It never gave me any problems at all. I am very happy with how this one is made. The pop up head is a nice feature and makes cleaning it easy. I also like having a push button to turn it on instead of sliding a switch. I am glad that I did not opt to buy anything more expensive because I don&#x27;t see how I&#x27;d be any more pleased.</li>
    <li> This is the shaver for those who would rather not use a standard razor. It gets really close and you don&#x27;t have press very hard to get a nice shave. Only press lightly. The motor does the rest. Great value for the money.</li>
    <li> I bought the Philips Norelco 7310 last summer and have purposely held off writing a review until I had had a chance to see the battery capacity and use it over a reasonable period. It lives up to its promises! I am very surprised by the comments of other reviewers that the battery capacity is not up to expectation. I have used the shaver every day over the course of months and have had to charge it only 5 times (almost a month per charge). The speed of the motor does seem unexpectedly slower than earlier examples of the type, but it does not affect the shave. Directions say that it can be washed under a stream of tap water to clean it and I have. That has seemed to cause no problem with the device. I have used it without problem both at home and on a sailboat (for weeks) in a salt-air environment. The shaver provides a quick close shave with little if any irritation. I hate to pass out 5-star ratings without solid justification, but this thing earns 5-stars. At the price point it is hard to beat this shaver.</li>
    <li> I got this a month ago, i let my skin get used to the razor before i reviewed it. Now i must say that the blades are VERY fragile when you open the top it can snap off instantly but you can snap it back on. Also this razor is very underpowered. What i mean by that is i have a 7 year old remington razor and the blades still work faster and i get a closer shave with it. This Philips Norelco i am only going to use as a back up because i cant see my self useing this razor daily.</li>
    <li> This shaver is the third Norelco model I&#x27;ve had in 15 years... and without question the best and closest shaving of all!  From the side grip ridges (surrounding the head) that give an additionally secure feel to the handling... to the wash-out feature that affords easiest clean-up the 7310 is topnotch at a reasonable price! Highly recommended!</li>
    <li> (Barbara&#x27;s other half)  I had an older Norelco shaver that I&#x27;m sure was at least 10 years old. I had to push in on the power button to get full speed out of it and I know the blades were shot. It took me a long time to get a poor shave. I considered replacing the blades, but with the power button problem, I decided to spring.  What the heck, it&#x27;s only $40, where the other rotary shavers are much more.  I can now get a decent shave in 1 1/2 minutes. I charged it when I first got it about a month ago and haven&#x27;t recharged it yet. Great product for the price so far.</li>
    <li> This is a powerful razor and well worth the value. My only complaints would be that it is not extremely close and also is not as powerful when not plugged in. Otherwise, it is recommended.</li>
    <li> Got it as a Christmas gift, arrived in a timely manner. My honey loves it, and looks as though I paid more than it&#x27;s worth!</li>
    <li> This shaver cuts almost as close as a wet shave.  I&#x27;m amazed at the power of the battery.  Since the initial charge, I  have had at least 5 shaves and it still doesn&#x27;t need a recharge yet.   Amazon&#x27;s shipping is also a plus.</li>
    <li> I have had many many electric razors from the expensive to the cheaper disposable head ones with the same results, DISAPPOINTMENT! But with this Philips Norelco I was pleasantly surprised. I bought it for a travel shaver when water &amp; my blades wouldn&#x27;t make sense but after using it for the 1st time I really found that I finally had a good razor that I could use all the time, toss the blades! It is really light weight &amp; comfortably conforms to even my ole scared up tough bearded face. I get a close shave , even those pesky hairs on my neck and by my ears!! what A DELIGHT THANKS norelco......</li>
    <li> I needed to replace the shaver heads on my corded Norelco.  I discovered that I could buy this new razor for about the same price as replacement heads on the old unit.  Also, the new razor has the added convenience of being cordless.  The new razor produces a similar shave as my old razor when the blades are new.  Also, like the previous razor, the smoothness improves after a few shaves as the blades settle in.  There are probably better razors out there but for this price....</li>
    <li> I received the shaver as scheduled, in manufacturer&#x27;s packaging. I&#x27;ve been using Norelco shavers for about 30 years, with complete satisfaction. The washable feature is very nice----just rinse it under the faucet. A full charge of the battery lasts me about 10 days. The price was 10 dollars less than CVS for the same unit.</li>
    <li> I&#x27;ve been a seasoned and avid Norelco electric razor fan for over 25 years (still own an old 5601X which I loaned to my son), must express genuine overall disappointment in this new model.  I&#x27;ve owned it for about 6 months now, and here are my impressions.  On the positive side, the 7310XL is light-weight and the rinsable feature is a practical plus; however, the negatives far outweigh the pros.  Unless I lucked out with one with an defective battery, my experience has been that after just a couple of uses (avg. 5-10 min. ea.), the razor starts to quickly lose power &amp; requires a recharge.  The quality of the shave itself is inferior to my previous Norelco&#x27;s, including the 5601X.  While it is quieter in operation, it invariably fails to provide a consistently smooth shave, leaving a scattering of hairs even after several passes.  I agree with other reviewers that it tends to be more abrasive on the skin, certainly in comparison to the 5601X and Braun models I&#x27;ve owned.  The plastic head cover is sturdy, but I don&#x27;t like the fact that it fails to cover the entire head assembly.  This model also doesn&#x27;t come with a travel/storage case.  It is moderately priced, but considering the Norelco reputation for excellent shavers, I only rate it as fair.  Oh, the trimmer is lame, failing to provide a close trim and inevitably tipping down when encountering any shape resistance.</li>
    <li> You can spend a lot more for an electric razor, but why should you?  This is my second Norelco shaver, and since my first, the technology has gotten better to provide an even closer shave! The new \\&quot;flip top\\&quot; design and the ability to rinse it under running water makes cleaning a breeze.</li>

    <li> I have used several Norelco shavers in the past and have always been impressed by their coverage, speed, comfort, ease of use and maintenance.  I have used both rotary and foil shavers and I have discovered that rotary usually does a better job overal to help me maintain my profile.    I&#x27;m a clean-cut guy who does not have a lot of facial hair to begin with so I don&#x27;t need an heavy duty shaver to suit my needs.  I own the Braun M90 (for traveling) and the Norelco 7310XL - both \\&quot;budget\\&quot; shavers at similar price range (under $50).  This is my 3rd Norelco that I have owned and the cheapest one I have ever used.  Overall, I am very happy with its performance and if I had a choice, I would always use the Norelco 7310XL over Braun M90.  I only use the Braun M90 as a backup if I ever run out of battery on the Norelco and its flat profile makes it one of the best travel shavers.  However, the Norelco 7310XL definitely provides better coverage, closer, faster shave and is more comfortable to use.      My first impression of Norelco 7310XL is that it is much lighter than the more expensive Norelco&#x27;s that I have owned.  I believe the main difference is in the motor inside as other shaving-specific mechanism are very similar to the higher end models.  The motor on this one is definitely weaker.  More motor power provides a faster and more comfortable shaving experience.  However, if you&#x27;re like me who shave once or twice daily, the 7310XL should be quite suitable as you&#x27;re not doing heavy duty shaving on a daily basis.  I also like the fact that you can clean the inside with water.      The battery life is superb.  Obviously it depends on how much hair you have but for me, one full charge which takes about 8 hours to charge should last you about one month.  From my personal experience, the battery actually lasts longer than the more expensive Norelco&#x27;s probably because it has a smaller motor.  There&#x27;s no battery level indicator but it shouldn&#x27;t be a problem for most people - when the battery is dead, just plug it into the wall and continue.  Overall, you will get a lot of mileage out of the Norelco 7310XL for light to moderate daily grooming.  Moreover, even if it happens to die after some time, you won&#x27;t feel sorry for your wallet or anger towards the manufacturer.  If you&#x27;re looking at dollar per shave, then you&#x27;ll probably find this to be one of the best deals around.  Highly recommended.</li>

If you skip a day of shaving, you&#x27;ll probably need to use the trimmer first. And that&#x27;s where the design flaw is; the trimmer is useless.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Previous models had a sliding activating mechanism that would lock the trimmer into place, preventing it from moving while you used it. This model relies on a spring mechanism to keep the trimmer engaged, making it extremely flimsy. Any pressure in the wrong direction and the trimmer folds back down. This makes trimming the hair on your neck almost impossible, and if you shower before you shave and have any residual moisture on your face, the trimmer can&#x27;t cut it.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;So while I am (at best) satisfied with the shave, this razor almost requires a separate trimmer to be of any value if you don&#x27;t plan on shaving every day religiously.</li>
    <li> Purchased this for my husband over a year ago. He shaves daily and has commented that he loves the close shave that this gives. He has sensitive skin and previous shavers have ripped his face up pretty good, but this hasn&#x27;t. Prior to this, I had purchased him a foil strip style shaver that broke after a year. He prefers the closeness of the rotary shaver over the strip. This is the first shaver he&#x27;s had that he doesn&#x27;t constantly complain about.     <li> I have had the Norelco 7310XL for a few weeks now, and overall, I&#x27;m pretty satisfied.  The shaver has good and not so good points, so let&#x27;s look at them.    Pros:    Very good shaving results on the relatively smooth, unobstructed parts of my face.  Cheeks, chin and the neck are where this shaver shines.  Just press lightly and move the shaver in a circular motion for a very close, quick and comfortable shave.    Light weight and very quiet in operation.  Much quieter than my old Braun shaver.    Good battery life.  Looks like the shaver will need a recharge no more than once per week.    The recharging cord is long enough to allow you to use this as a corded shaver while it is recharging.  That&#x27;s a real convenience if you are in a hurry and find that your shaver battery is dead.    Easy to clean.  Just pop the top open, and rinse with hot water.    Cons:    The ergonomics of the shaving head leave a lot to be desired.  The shaving head is big and bulky, and that makes it very awkward when you are trying to shave relatively small areas like your upper lip.  This is the major drawback of this Norelco (and probably all rotary-type shavers), and I still often use my old Braun foil-type shaver on my lip.    You must follow Norelco&#x27;s instructions EXACTLY when shaving tender areas, such as your neck.  Specifically, do not press the shaver too hard against your skin.  If you do, you will be rewarded with Olympic-size skin irritation.  I can personally vouch for the truth of this statement.    &#x3D;&#x3D;&#x3D;&#x3D;&#x3D;&#x3D;&#x3D;&#x3D;&#x3D;&#x3D;&#x3D;&#x3D;&#x3D;&#x3D;&#x3D;&#x3D;&#x3D;&#x3D;&#x3D;&#x3D;&#x3D;&#x3D;&#x3D;&#x3D;&#x3D;&#x3D;&#x3D;&#x3D;&#x3D;&#x3D;    I bought this shaver when my old Braun Free Control 1775 shaver began to show signs of needing a replacement shaving head, and I found that the price of the shaving head was too close to the price of a complete new shaver.  So, I thought I would try this Norelco, which is in approximately the same price range as my Braun.  i.e.  They are both on the cheap end of their product lines.    The bottom line on this Norelco is that it does some things reallywell, like shaving my cheeks and neck.  It does these areas better and more quickly than my Braun foil-type shaver.  But, the Norelco does some things badly, like shaving my upper lip.  The Braun 1775 shaver&#x27;s head gets into tight areas much better, but shaving is slower and noisier overall with the Braun.    The real issue here is probably whether you like rotary or foil-type shavers.  Both can be very good, but only at some aspects of shaving your face.  As far at this particular Norelco goes, it seems to be a pretty good representative of the rotary type of shaver.  If you like rotary shavers, this Norelco is probably as good as any.    Whatever faults this Norelco may have seem to be common to all rotary shavers, and not because of any defect in this particular model.  So, don&#x27;t throw your money at the more expensive Norelcos, thinking that they will be better.  You won&#x27;t change the nature of the beast, you will just be getting a nicer looking beast with more bells and whistles.</li>

    <li> Amazon had a great deal on this shaver so I decided to give it a try. My first electric shaver (from many years ago) was a Norelco rotary head. I used it for many years before eventually switching to a straight blade razor to get a closer shave. I have somewhat sensitive skin so I get easily irritated if I use a straight razor every day. Hence, about 10 years ago I started using an electric shaver every other day and a regular straight razor with shaving cream on the days in between. (This eliminated the problems I was experiencing.)  I have owned and tried many different electric razors over my 30+ years of shaving and have never encountered one that shaves as close as a straight razor with shaving cream. This makes sense if you think about it because with an electric razor there is always some kind of &#x27;guard&#x27; between the blades and the skin. With a regular straight razor the blade is riding right on your skin. Anybody expecting an electric razor to shave as close as a blade is in for a disappointment -- and the Norelco 7310 is no different. Hence, I wasn&#x27;t expecting a close shave, but I was pleasantly surprised at how good of a shave I did get! My beard is not very thick (medium density), but the hairs are very coarse and tough. After use, I usually used a straight razor to dispose of this growth.  The 7310, much to my surprise, does a perfect job on the beard and the neck.  I would say that my morning shave now takes less than two minutes.    Hints:  I always use Williams Lectric shave prior to shaving and I have to stretch my skin slightly to help the razor glide over the beard.  The first two times I used the 7310 I felt some slight irritation on my neck after shaving. By the third day the irritation was gone. The manual states it takes some time for your face to adjust to the razor.  They are correct.    The 7310 comes with a two year warrantee. I suspect the unit will not last as long as my old one, but that seems to be true of all products today.      For the price, this was an excellent purchase.  I can&#x27;t see how spending more money would get me a better shave.  Go for it.</li>
    <li> Pros:  Very close and comfortable shave  Excellent sideburn trimmer  Good battery life  Charge completed flashing LED&#x27;s  Price is right if . . .    Cons:  No battery status indication, none expected  Tacky colors    I&#x27;ve been shaving for over forty years, mostly electric and mostly Norelco. For 3-months I had a Remington R450, see my review, huge dissapointment. Every couple of years Norelco tries to come up with a new gimmick to get us to purchase the latest and greatest. Thing is that Norelco got it right 30-years ago. The cutters and combs in the 7310 are the essence of that technology and if you can spin the cutters you&#x27;ll have a close shave. All the other Whistles &amp; Bells are just fluff.    Norelco claims 10 days of cordless shaving on a 8-hour charge. The charge full indicator started flashing at 2-hours, done. I went 9-days and wondered how much longer, on the tenth day the motor started slowing down and it quit halfway through the eleventh day. By stretching the battery after the first charge/discharge I was able to get 12-days, well actually 11.9-days, could have used another minute of shaving. I stretch a NiCd by running the battery dead with the cutters flipped open for the lowest motor load. Pretty impressive for a single AA NiCd battery.    People claim this is a good/great budget shaver. Nonsense, this is a excellent cordless shaver that can be had at a budget price. I got mine from the big W for thirty-one to my PO Box. It came in the full retail blister pack. By the time I got it to my house, 8500-feet, I thought it was going to explode. I saw at least two retailers have it for a bit less on Black Friday. Makes you wonder what the models that cost 4-5 times as much have to offer?    So why is it ugly? Well of course beauty is in the eye of the beholder and this old eye doesn&#x27;t do black and white on a shaver, all black . . sure, all white . . probably not, all silver like my deceased 7865XL&#x27;s . . YES!!! I still gave the 7310 5-stars, I don&#x27;t see the colors while shaving. BTW, I do like the white power switch.    If you look at the photos I posted, you&#x27;ll see that the 7310 consists of a small waterproof power module encased in four cosmetic shells. It&#x27;s these shells that allow Norelco to play the silly color games at no additional cost. The sides even have rubber bonded to the shell. Turns out I shave with my thumb between the power switch and head and my fingers over the trimmer, so I don&#x27;t even feel the \\&quot;slip proof\\&quot; rubber. Where are your fingers?    So if the feature set meets your needs, don&#x27;t hesitate to get the 7310, it will deliver a comfortable close shave. As to the colors, only you can decide.</li>

Shaving 90 degrees to growth will catch much less frequently, then once you&#x27;ve removed most of the hair shave against like normal to finish.    Once you figure this out so it won&#x27;t nick you so much after a couple days between, this is a relatively good shaver for the money.</li>

I gave it 4 stars because it needs a battery gauge, what you see in the picture under the word charge is just that an indicator.  You plug the unit and the charge light comes on, it stays on solid green until the unit is charged and then it flashes green.  But once you unplug it you never see the indicator again until you charge it again (about weekly).  The obvious problem is that you never know the amount of charge left in the battery.  At home this isn&#x27;t a big problem as you can plug it in and shave with it while it is plugged in.  However grabbing it on the way out the door and jumping in the car is less reliable.  My solution is to charge the battery every Monday morning, so it hasn&#x27;t been a problem for me yet.    Yes I can recommend this shaver, and when the time comes I might just get a little better model (based on the shaving heads used in the model).  I&#x27;m not complaining about the heads in this unit, but looking at the different replacement blades from Norelco I can see that some of the other ones have more slots for shaving. For me, it is back to my normal razor.</li>

As of this review, this product has 837 reviews:  437 five-star, 238 four-star, 78 three-star, 40 two-star, and 44 one-star.  With ratings like that, I thought this would be a great-value and a decent razor at a good price. I did my research and I was still wrong. I have also owned the [[ASIN:B001FA1F8K Braun Series 1  1-150 Men&#x27;s Shaver]] and the [[ASIN:B003YJB026 Braun Series 5-550cc Shaver System, Black and Silver]] (it was a gift). I have shaved with this thing for 30-days and see no improvement in my face \\&quot;getting used to it\\&quot; nor in the cutting performance. If the thing would cut the hair on my face, maybe I would quibble about such things.  Since it does not cut, my recommendation is to keep looking.     <li> This is my third Norelco shaver.  I bought the first on around 2000 for $100+, the second came from Amazon in 2006.  Both succumbed to the same issue - battery age.  The NIMH battery battery pack Norelco uses is good for about 5 years, after which it pretty much stops taking charge.  Replacing it would be a snap, it is really just to AA rechargeables, if Norelco did not solder the battery pack, so if you want to keep your shaver, you either have to service it (expensive!) or learn to use soldering iron.  My solution, then and now was to replace the entire shaver.  It particularly makes sense with this one - it is cheaper than the pack of the replacement heads!&lt;br /&gt;So, the positives:  it is cheap.  Really, I paid $28 for it, and a set of HQ6 heads for my old shaver is 30.  It makes not sense at all but nevertheless that&#x27;s how Philips pricing works.  It looks and feels good, in my opinion black and white scheme makes it sleek and modern.  It shaves well, it is just as good any other Norelco shaver - if you used one before, and liked it you won&#x27;t be disappointed.  The charger slot is the same as on older models.&lt;br /&gt;Now, the negatives, all minor things, really.  First of all, I really miss LCD screen of my old shaver which showed the remaining charge.  I thought I would and I do, so if this is something you find very useful this may not be a shaver for you.  Looks are cool, but a rubbery grip is an absolute magnet for hair.  The charger connection is not 100% reliable, after the first few times it lost connection from being moved during charging I learned to double-check.  There&#x27;s no travel bag.  Not really a negative, but it is 1.5 oz lighter than my old shaver and felt sounded like a cheap plastic toy a few first times, before I got used to it.&lt;br /&gt;So, in the end - do I regret buying it? Not for a second!  But 5 years from now, assuming I still can afford electricity, I may go for a more upscale model.</li>

    <li> Received mine about three weeks ago. Even though the manual included recommends giving it three weeks for your skin to adjust, my skin adjusted very quickly and the unit produced excellent results from day one. The battery life is surprisingly good: a single charge lasted long enough for daily shaves of 2-3 minutes for almost two weeks. The charge-full indicator is also good: the flashing reliably lets me know when to unplug the unit. The sideburn trimmer is nothing special but works OK. Cleaning the unit is nice and easy (just hold it under a running hot tap). The quality of the shave itself is easily en par with shaving using an ordinary safety razor, if not a little better because it&#x27;s more consistent. It also copes better than a safety razor does with coarse hair e.g. on one&#x27;s neck.    Other reviewers have described feeling that the machine is pulling out their hairs rather than cutting them: this hasn&#x27;t been the case for me. It hasn&#x27;t been painful at all shaving daily. I *did* however notice what they describe if I let my beard become too long - more than, say, 2mm - before using the unit. (This happens mostly around the tip of the sideburns.) So: 1. Use the sideburn trimmer to avoid longish hairs before using the shaver proper. 2. If your beard is longer than a couple of millimetres, shave using something else first? I haven&#x27;t experimented properly to find out what&#x27;s best to do in that situation, yet.    This machine has made shaving much, much more pleasant for me, to the extent that daily shaving is now part of my routine (previously, it was too much effort). If and when this unit wears out (no sign of that yet!) I&#x27;ll be buying this brand again.</li>

    <li> I bought this product based on the reviews here at Amazon and am happy with my purchase.  I particularly appreciate the many reviewers who have had several other electric shavers at various price points and stressed that in terms of just the shave, this Norelco was on par with top of the line shavers that cost $100+ more.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;This is my first electric shaver, so I cannot provide such comparisons.  I would, though, like to point out a few things that I didn&#x27;t see in previous reviews that might help others make a decision.  First, although this is an electric shaver and cannot possibly provide as close of a shave as the ones that use razor blades, I was impressed at just how close the shave is with the 7310XL.  As is pointed out in the instruction booklet, which I guess many people ignore, it helps if you stretch your skin with your non-shaving hand.  Also, make sure your skin is dry and be sure to shave against the grain.  Finally, don&#x27;t press too hard or it may pinch your skin (another tip of the instruction manual).  Using this four-pronged technique, I am able to get an impressively smooth shave.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;My biggest concern was shaving around my jaw bone (I&#x27;m quite skinny so don&#x27;t have the benefit of a nice round jaw line).  While this does take longer to shave than the rest of my face combined, I was able to get a satisfactory shave here too.  Lastly, I have sensitive skin, so was worried about irritation; several reviewers mentioned that this was an issue for them.  I actually found the irritation to be mild (no worse for me than with a blade-based razor).  And, by just splashing a little warm water on my face I was able to alleviate the little itchiness that I did feel.  Note: the instructions also point out that irritation is common in the beginning and should subside within the first 21 days of exclusive use.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;I hope this helps.  Happy shaving!</li>

    <li> ****Please note that I decided to tighten and revise this review, as I have had this razor for several years.  I would now give it 4 stars for quality, 5 stars for value.  My initial opinion was too negative.  This shaver provides a fairly standard Norelco (i.e. 3 head rotary shaver) shave.  This is my third Norelco (well second, but I bought a third one recently), and by far the lowest priced one I&#x27;ve owned.  If you like the Norelco shave, I think this is an excellent value.  Of course, many prefer the Braun/Phillips type single head razors, but it seems there is no way to tell who will prefer which.  If you have never tried a Norelco, this would be a good model to try because of the low price.  I now have an 8345 (which is the same as the 8340 but comes with extra heads) in addition to this one.  The 8345 may be more money and newer, but they look, feel and shave fairly similarly.  8345 has more holes on the heads (can only be good I guess) but the motor sounds like it runs a lot slower.  They seem to shave about as well, but the cheaper 7310 actually seems a bit gentler on the face (maybe because the 8345 has more holes but runs slower).  The 7310 feels generally solid enough and comfortable in the hand.  Feels like all the Norelco&#x27;s do, more or less.  The pop up trimmer seems reasonably solid, and functions like all of these pop-up trimmers do.  It will shave your sideburns, but you may or may not be satisfied with it.  Nature of the beast.  The plug is also a little on the large side, which could be an issue for traveling, though not that bad really.  I dont think it came with a travel case, but I could have misplaced it.  The battery cannot be changed easily because its welded in.  At $40-50 for the razor, I suppose that is not a huge issue, but its not a plus factor either.  I think this is true of all Norelcos.  This razor does hold a charge for quite a while, its good for several shaves without a recharge.  However, there is no charge indicator at all.  There is a green light that comes on when the razor is on, and another green light when its plugged in, but nothing changes as the battery gets low that I can see.  You know it needs a charge when the motor starts to slow.  A 5 or 10 minute emmergency charge is fine, so its not a great problem.  About the only difference between this razor and the $100+ Norelco I used to own was that the expensive one had a battery charge indicator.  Maybe there was more metal and less plastic in the more expensive one, but...so what?  I have had this razor for 2 1/2 years, and use it about every other day.  Maybe the battery doesnt last as long and the heads are duller, but its nothing I notice.  I have put 0 money in it, and it still works well and compares well to my other electric razors.  Verdict:  good shaver if you like Norelco&#x27;s, and a bargain at $40-50.  Spending more money is recommended if you want a batter charge indicator, but beyond that, not clear to me what you get for your extra money.  If you like the Braun-type razors better, I dont know of any reason why this one would convert you, but I can otherwise recommend this razor pretty strongly.</li>

That being said, the thing still works pretty well and the only reason I decided it was time for a new one was that the battery has started to go and doesn&#x27;t hold a charge very long. I knew that a screen shaver was not for me, and I&#x27;ve had good experience with Norelco, which lead me to this shaver.  I read many reviews on the 7310 and other similar items and settled on this one mostly due to the good reviews and cost.  At the time there was an online coupon for $10, bringing the price down to $20.  I was a bit disappointed when I powered it on (after full charge) and could barely hear the motor.  I have a thick beard so I was hoping that a new shaver would have some noise to it, and I suppose my assumption was that the louder, the more powerful.  I have to say that although the motor does sound weak, it shaves surprisingly well and close.  In fact, I normally use a combo of electric and razor - electric to go around some bumps and then a traditional razor for that extra close shave.  During the first couple weeks, the shave has been so close that I couldn&#x27;t justify breaking out the shaving cream and razor, it just wasn&#x27;t necessary.  I also like the fact that the heads are waterproof and can be cleaned under a faucet. I&#x27;ve been using the razor for two weeks and so far am very pleased.  I give it 4 stars only because I reserve 5 stars for items that completely blow me away beyond my expectations.  This item didn&#x27;t knock my socks off, but it is a great value for the money and I highly recommend it.</li>

    <li> This razor works great. It cuts close, and the charge lasts for a long time. It is easy to use, and the charge lasts a long time. The shaver also has a pop-up trimmer in the back. It comes with a small two-sided brush for cleaning, and a plastic cover to keep dust out of the heads.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;The shaver uses a special patented technology to cut hair closer to the skin. The process involves two blades; one pulls the hair partly out of the skin, and the other cuts it. Once it&#x27;s cut, the hair retreats back into the skin, resulting in a nice close shave. According to the manufacturer, your skin needs to adjust to the new shaving style for the shaver to work the way it&#x27;s supposed to. This could take a week or two (depending on how often you shave).&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;As with many razors, the batteries are not removable; you charge it by plugging it into either a 100V or 240V AC outlet using the included adapter. Don&#x27;t charge the razor if the indoor temperature is above 95, or the lifetime of the batteries could be reduced.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;To clean the shaver, the instruction manual says to turn it off and unplug it, and then open the top and rinse inside the hair chamber with hot water, as well as both sides of the heads. Leave it open to dry. If you don&#x27;t feel comfortable using water, use the included brush. The manual says to clean the pop-up trimmer after each use, using the brush (instead of water).</li>

    <li> I bought this Phillips Norelco 7310 at Best Buy for $30, even less than was advertised on their web site.  Maybe it was the last one in stock and they needed the shelf space. I was going to return it but decided I would give it a chance.  What a loss! How does anyone get these shavers with these tiny holes to work?  It was not even a good on short hairs and after a few days it was returned to the store.  Then, a week of comparing reviews led me to this shaver.  I was determined no to pay upwards of a hundred dollars for a shaver.  I really lucked out on price.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Now, the review.  Four stars because I am so happy that right out of the box with a couple of days growth, it shaved really really close - like a new razor.  It is as good or better in terms of close shave as any of the other dozen or so I have had in the last three or four decades.  It took the full eight hours to charge, but it does work as a corded shaver if you forget to charge up.  It lasted around two weeks on that first charge. This works well even for a little trim of my head hair, so thumbs up on that performance. Last point is that is was easy to clean and I also like that it is washable though I don&#x27;t wash it.  So, my basic review is that is does everything it is supposed to do and does it well and maintains a charge and is modestly priced.  Four stars, and now, why not five?&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;I had to get used to the \\&quot;heft\\&quot; of this shaver.  Why complain because it is light you ask?  Well, it feels like a cheaper plastic and that gives me concerns about how durable it is.  My old ones had a weight that felt substantial in your hand and a thick shell. For all the times I dropped it or missed when throwing it in the suitcase, I never had one of these break on me.  In recent years I have found so many products with half the weight and made with less and cheaper materials in China that I now save every receipt because so many once-substantial products now fall apart.  Maybe I&#x27;ll make an addendum to this review after a year of use. Same applies to the length of time the blades last. I am expecting no noticeable deterioration for a year. As an aside, the speed of rotation of the heads seems slower and probably quieter than past experience.  I did not notice a slower speed  having a negative impact on effectiveness in shaving and I guess it aides battery life, but it took a little getting used to. So, negatives are the \\&quot;Made in China\\&quot; feel and the cost of replacement blades, both of which will take a year to decide if the value is really there.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Bottom line is I got a very good product for the price and think it is versatile enough to suit most men.s that is was easy to clean and I also like that it is washable though I don&#x27;t wash it.     <li> I also have the norelco 7340. This shaver the 7310 has a smoother screen consisting of only round holes for hairs and it exhibits less tendency to cause nicks. The 7340 has some rectangular slots to catch the longer hairs easier and the 7340 does shave quicker. However, the 7340 has a much higher chance of cutting top layers of skin (aka nicks) with the larger rectangular slot.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;The 7310 is my preferred daily shaver.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;The 7340 is my preferred shaver after 2 or more days without shaving.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;AFTER 1 YEAR;&lt;br /&gt;After 1 year, the two shavers heads became dull and replacement cost of the head almost equals cost of complete razor and heads if on sale.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;The solution is to revert to the old shaver technology prior to floating heads. Many of us have had the older norelco shavers. I first watched a traveling guy who would go to towns and \\&quot;tune up\\&quot; their old norelco shavers. This consisted of light removing of hairs and a drop of oil along with the most important task of sharpening the heads.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;How did he do it? Quite simply by pressing the metal screen against a hairless finger tip or palm of this hand. Now you just need to apply this to your shaver. But wait. You have a floating head which prevents the force needed to push metal against metal (screen and rotating shavers)and thus sharpen both.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Solution: Remove the plastic that isolates the 3 heads, rinse in water, dry, apply glue of choice (I used cyanoacrylate) and then I waited 30 minutes and reinserted into shaver. This prevents the heads from moving much. Next turn on the shaver and apply finger pressure to one head at a time. After a few minutes all 3 heads are close to as sharp as new and your finished.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Life is a risk and your walk may not end as well as mine. Hope you have a good journey and good luck.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;P.S. If I were a manufacturer of shavers. Putting in floating heads to prevent sharpening while flaunting the virtues of going around facial obstacles with less chance of nicking skin is and was a brilliant idea.</li>

I returned it and found this one on sale for $30 after coupon. Some reviewers have said the 7310 has a NiCad battery, whereas others noted that it had a Li-ion battery. Mine came in a box that said \\&quot;Green High Energy LI-ION\\&quot; on the bottom. This probably contributes to the shaver feeling very lightweight. Also, I noticed that while the box said \\&quot;Philips Norelco 7310\\&quot; on it, the actual shaver is a [[ASIN:B00302T2CM Norelco 7315xl]]. It&#x27;s really too bad that the battery indicator flashes to indicate a fully charged battery. Furthermore, it would be useful if the razor would stop charging automatically once the battery is full to prevent overcharging, as this kills battery life.     <li> Let me start out by saying that I was really angered by the amount of packaging this shaver came in.  It came in a cardboard box, and inside that was a sealed plastic clam-shell that you have to use heavy scissors to cut through, and inside of that there was more plastic and cardboard.  One would think that a large, modern company (especially a European company) would be more environmentally conscious.  The good news is that the clear plastic that non-food products come packaged in can now be recycled with your cans and bottles in many, if not most, localities.  If you buy a product that comes in a bubble glued to a piece of cardboard, you should separate the two and then recycle the plastic with your cans and bottles and the cardboard with your paper and cardboard (the economics of recycling don&#x27;t allow recyclers to pay someone to separate plastic from cardboard, so you need to do that yourself).&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;I&#x27;ve been using Norelco shavers for 40 years.  This shaver is both better and worse than their older shavers.  The actual shaving performance is much better.  I have an older plug-in Norelco shaver, and, while shaving, I have to rub my face a couple times with a hot washcloth to raise my whiskers.  I don&#x27;t have to raise my whiskers with this new shaver, meaning that I can shave my face dry and get a close shave.  In fact, the shave is so close that it leaves my skin a little sore.  (In actual practice, I still drag a hot, moist washcloth across my face to make sure all my whiskers are raised.)  This shaver is also very quiet, so it doesn&#x27;t hurt my ears.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;On the down side, the trimmer doesn&#x27;t work as well as the plug-in shaver that I already own.  It doesn&#x27;t take hair off as well, and it doesn&#x27;t stand out at a far enough angle.  Also, the shaver part will sometimes pull long hairs instead of cutting them off, and that can be painful.  In my opinion, both the trimmer performance and the tendency to pull hairs is due to this being a battery-operated shaver, meaning that the cutters don&#x27;t have as much power behind them as a plug-in shaver.  Plug-in shavers have more robust performance, but they are louder.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;I can&#x27;t tell you how many shaves the charge is good for because I shave every 5 days.  I get three shaves out a charge, but then I shave much longer than if I were shaving every day.  If the shaver loses it charge during a shave, you&#x27;ll have to plug it in and wait five minutes for it to charge slightly before continuing.  You then have to complete your shave with the plug in.  One good thing is that Norelco shavers now come with straight cords instead of a coiled cords.  The coiled cords were a nuisance.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;I have some concerns about the on/off button.  It is one of those soft, molded plastic buttons that deforms when you push it (instead of a normal mechanical switch).  My experience with such buttons is that the plastic eventually fatigues and cracks.  I doubt it will last as long as the rest of the shaver lasts.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;In short:  great shaving performance, so-so pop-up trimmer, environmentally unfriendly packaging.</li>
